<Author>Camelduece
<Content>Location is the best for the price Just got back from a wonderful two week 3 Island Hawaiian Honeymoon. We flew into Honolulu because it was cheaper.We booked the High Ocean View-Ocean Promotion for $149 a night during our Honeymoon around Christmas. Best value around for the price and location is great. Stayed for 3 nights, and would not suggest any longer.We were in the tower on floor 20 on diamond head side which is better. If you book it, just call ahead and request it.The buffet smell was so pungent that it reached into the lobby and slapped you in the face. We never ate anything from the hotel. We suggest finding a nice restaurant in Wakiki, money better spent.Parking is $20 bucks a day, although all the hotels get at at least that a day for parking.Overall I would suggest it for a short stay. Great location!

<Author>abbey_315
<Content>Would not recommend The location was pretty good as the hotel is in the midst of everything, and pretty much across the street from the beach.We stayed in the older part of the hotel and it is ghetto!! We were with a group and some of the other people were in the newer part which was an improvement, but not great, but what you would probably expect for the price. Our room/ wing is BADLY in need of a remodel or tear down. I think the bathroom is literally from 1950... the toilet is the kind that you get at a publlic restroom that you flush with your foot... the bathroom was not clean and it was gross. I did not want to take my sandals off and walk barefoot on the gross floor. The sheets were incredibly scratchy. The tv barely worked-- we constantly had lines and static, also it was an old 19 inch tv. The room was tiny as well. You might think that the room doesn't matter much since you don't go to hawaii to stay in your room... well, we thought the same, but it ended up being really rainy (pouring) for several days so we were stuck inside. The pool is pretty small and closes at 6pm. Parking cost us $200!!!! We didn't eat at the buffet in the hotel-- it was $40/per person and did NOT look worth it.. we instead went to a really nice steakhouse for the same price. Also, there is no spa at the hotel. Overall, I would definitely not recommend this hotel to anyone... I think there are nicer hotels for the same price range. We thought the fact that it is a Sheraton would help and make it nicer... disappointment. The staff seemed pretty friendly though.

<Author>oldhousegirl
<Content>Excellent Value very near the beach For $129 a block from the beach, I have no complaints. The staff was very friendly, and without asking we got our Starwood Gold upgrade to a partial oceanview room. From our balcony we were able to enjoy the nightly live entertainment by the pool.My one complaint about the hotel is the slowness of the elevators. We had a very large group staying in our tower, and we often waited a very long time to ride in a jam-packed elevator.The fitness room is quite large, clean, and with decent equipment. We never ate the breakfast buffet, though it looked quite good, because we walked a couple of blocks to Duke's (on the water) for their excellent $15 buffet. We did eat the dinner buffet ($40) one night during the live show -- average, but we just didn't want to go out and wanted to see the show. You're only a block away from the beach, and we sat in the reserved area for the other Sheratons that are right on the beach. It certainly didn't see worth paying $100 more to avoid a short walk. This hotel is also right next to International Marketplace and lots of other shops and restaurants. Our room was clean and our Sheraton Sweet Sleeper bed wonderful.

<Author>akworldtraveler
<Content>Book the cheapest room and get a 12" tv First of all, this was my 7th stay at the PK. The rooms and service have certainly improved. This is a tourist class hotel. Don't be mislead by any website's star rating. It is a solid three at times and a meager two at others, but not a bit more or less. The people who posted the worst pictures paid the least. In an ideal word this shouldn't be, but in the world where we exchange money for services it really is. Even SPG rates it a cat 3 out of highest 7(not five).Don't expect to book the cheapest room on the block in a tourist class hotel in this area of waikiki and expect luxury. If you pay for a standard, expect one. They will usually move you to a better room if they have space to improve your experience. Sign up to be an SPG member beforehand and book through their site, their price guarantee is good. It is a large hotel, something like 1100 rooms, and has varying levels of comfort. There is the tower, 29 floors, sweet sleepers, flat screen tvs. The ocean view odd number rooms don't get much sun, but the even numbered ones do. There are very comfortable suites on the top two floors called 'series 71' and 'series 82'. But there can be housekeeping issues in the suites as well-once, we actually looked up at the ceiling lights over the bed, suite, 2871, and there were giant balls of dust around the lights, The a/c vents were nasty, and mold in the bathroom tile grout. But, in general, basic housekeeping is efficient. I don't think the maids climb up on beds to dust the 10' ceilings. Almost all rooms in this building have some sort of ocean view above the 12th floor. Four elevators generally very quick.There is the middle building, I think 12 floors, which has sweet sleepers, but I don't think flat screens yet. On the highest floors of this building are various suites of varying quality. Here you are directly across from the pool, with a good view of the Westin Moana and an ocean view if you are far enough up. On the backside you are out of luck. You are low to the street and the noise can be brutal, and quite frankly the view stinks. On the city side there are no lanais.And there is the wing on the right of check-in, usually reserved as 'crew' rooms for flight crews and 'bulk group tourist getting the cheapest rate' types. These are your two star rooms which have no sweet sleeper, 12 inch tvs, and even the sinks are on two aluminum stands(you can actually lift the sink up). The housekeeping is generally good because they need the aircrew business. The rooms are old but amazingly efficient with fantastic use of spaces. But this building is really your last choice.I've also heard of something called the annex, with extra cheap rooms, but I've never risked it.Contrary to what some other reviewer posted, there is room service. There just isn't any past 2130. A small pot of coffee adds up to about $9.53 by the time the service fee (17%) and deliver fee ($3) get added on. And the breakfast is a bit expensive by the time you add on coffee and juice. But people order room service for a reason so if you want to splurge-splurge, and don't complain.The prime rib buffet is always good downstairs, but I think it gets a bit expensive for everyday. There is always as much snow crab as one can eat. They always offer a seafood, poultry, and pork option in the buffet. There is always a pasta choice. And it's a good opportunity to try some japanese style salads, sushi(very limited), and tofu's. There is always a good selection of breads. There is a very good selection of fresh locally made deserts. The usual ice cream bar and melon and pineapple choices round out the dinner buffet. There are also a-la-carte options to choose from. There is also the requisite Waikiki hula show, every night.The breakfast buffet is interesting. You can have anything made to order by just asking-they don't tell you this, but I've done it several times. One can also treat oneself to the japanese style breakfast. Most people are the usual bacon and egg type so they pay for the buffet and complain there are no choices and it's not worth the 22 bucks per person. But there aren't many places where one can get 'all you can eat' salmon for breakfast or fermented soy beans with mustard. Momoya can be great, just be prepared for smaller portions. The service is good, it seems to me the same staff have been there for a few years. The prices are reasonable.The pikake lounge. Well, what can I say? Land of leisure suit Larry's and lounge lizards. Kidding. The staff are obviously union and not worried about being fired for customer complaints. They understandably don't remember all their clients, but as a returning client I certainly remember them all. They can be downright rude. I've waited 25 minutes for a server to even acknowledge my presence. And I've had to put up with several of them giving me attitude or just plain non-chalance. The drink qualities are inconsistent, invariably. But then again there have been times where they have been downright fantastic.Hint, if you want to have a few drinks at one of the partner hotels, compare prices for drinks and apps with those at the PK. The menus are the same, but the prices about 20% lower at PK.The front desk staff is there to help. There are times when they can be short, but, in general, they are friendly. They always seem to have a way to help me with my issues. There was a time when the front desk supervisor and a few of the clerks were miserable sods, but they seem to have all moved on to greener pastures. I tend to remember people by name. Good job Sherri, James, June, Shauna. Not so good job new guy working nights(forgetful) and day-girl whose name sounds like the Indian word for tea but slightly different(very short). Always, Always, Always, check your bill before you leave. I had the experience, three years ago, of having them (their accounting department) contact me 7 months after my stay to say they hadn't charged me fully!!! Stick up for yourself, but don't be rude to them, ie realize that although this is your vacation it's their job(tourist class hotel, not five star)The pool is there, always clean, lifeguard on duy, and always colder than the ocean. The towel and chair attendants are always great except the female whose name begins with Y. Never had luck with her. Sign in and out for towels with your room key. Really cool new thing is the ability to sign out beach chairs for the day. These have to be back by 1730 or kept till the next day, but they stop taking them back at 1730 no matter what.The Hotel location is fantastic. The public beaches are right across the street. The Westin, Royal Hawaiian(currently closed for renovation), and Sheraton Waikiki beaches are also available for PK customer use.There is a fee for internet, around $14 and change per day. Tough to find wireless, but if you are on the oceanside of the tower you can pick up the new Apple store's wireless. Or you can sign up with the skywave and have wireless everywhere, it's much cheaper than hotel internet. Forget about using the phones.Overall the hotel is dated and nowhere near the quality of her sisters along the beach. But it is a family friendly hotel. We stay here because we're platinum SPG - thus we can book a low-medium priced room and expect the upgrade, although that's also no guarantee.

<Author>AussieBecs
<Content>Great location and great for the price (comparitively) Stayed for three nights and loved every minute.We actually booked a standard room with 2 double beds and was not expecting much at all. When checking in we were advised that we'd been upgraded to a pool view room with king bed.We had room 712 and it was fabulous - great view of the pool, the Moana Surfrider across the street and also some ocean view. The room was tastefully decorated and updated - had the most comfortable (king) bed I've ever slept in. Was like sleeping on a cloud. The room also had a small 2 seater couch, desk, wardrobe with iron and safe (at a charge!), TV and large mini fridge.The bathroom was smallish but lots of towels and shower over bath. The shower had good pressure but when filling the bath the water didn't seem to get hot enough.The lanai had two chairs and a table, which was great to sit out on at night and listen to the music playing from the pool side.We were actually staying as part of our honeymoon, and returning to our room on the second day we had a lovely bottle of sparkling wine waiting for us, which was really nice and thoughtful.The pool is a good size and there are lots of lounge chairs to sit on. The strange thing is that the pool is incredibly deep - starts at a meter and then goes to almost 2 meters deep. the water was over my head after leaving one end of the pool by a meter or so. In otherwords, watch your kids - there is no kids pool either.Lobby was huge and lots of internet stations. The concierge can give you a great little bus route map and the travel desk always seemed busy and not very helpful.Front desk people were always really nice. Checking out was very quick.One thing I would fault is that the in room safe is charged at $3.25 per day! The location is superb - walking distance to anywhere and the bus stop to either the USS Arizona memorial or Hanauma Bay (or anywhere for that matter) is just around the corner.I really liked this hotel - i've stayed at the Moana Surfrider before, and also the Ohana West around the corner. For the room price and location, I was really impressed and would definetly stay again!

<Content>Great Location, Great Staff, Everything Else Just So-So For all of you out there curious about the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani here's the scoop.1st: The hotel is in a great location. <Content>loved the sheraton have just returned from a 12 night stay at the sheraton and cannot agree with the bad comments that are written about this hotel.ROOMSwe had a room on the 10th floor which was a good size and clean. there wasnt any mould in the bathroom clean towels everyday. yes the furniture is dated but it is clean and not falling apart.iron and board ,hair dryer, coffee maker are also in the room. the swimming pool is a nice area to sit round with enough sunbeds to go round. towels are provided.there is nice seating area for lunch and a beer but it is a bit expensive compared to a lot of places in waikiki. the breakfast buffet is very expensive and so is the dinner menu. but you are on holiday plenty of places to go and eat with various priced menus. cheese cake factory is superbthe location of this hotel is superb, right in the middle of waikiki with the beach just across the road. loads of excellant shops with a big shopping centre 15mins away on the bus.you do get a lot of cabin crew including captains staying at the hotel which i see as a good sign when booking a hotel. so if u want a 5 star hotel,go and book the outrigger across the road at twice the price. but if u want a reasonable priced hotel right smack in the middle of everything which is clean and tidy this is the place to stay.

<Content>Old Building/Great Location This was my third stay at this place. In the past, I always though the rooms and the halls could use some massive update/renovations. However, I was able to find a $130/night on Expecia, so I thought ok, one more time.Upon my checkin, they put me on the 5th floor on the old building (right of the checkin and they claimed it was an upgrade). Very old. I had to turn the shower head to massage mode to stop the high-pitch sound.Having said this, this hotel is very centrally located. In the heart of Waikiki Beach and close to hip bars and resturants. Yes, the hooker corner exits. It cracks me up but I coud see older folks being offended.So if you're looking for an ordinary, old hotel that has great value then this could be it. However, if you're looking for a fancier hotel with the frills, this isn't it.

<Author>sun0484
<Content>Great Hotel, Perfect Location! The hotel is situated perfectly across the street from Waikiki right on the main road, Kalakua. Although it is right off the main drag, you cannot hear the street noise. Live entertainment every night is great. You can relax by the pool, the bar, or in the restuarant and listen to the music and watch the hula dancing. Everything is very close by, within walking distance from the hotel. The staff at the hotel were all extremely friendly and helpful. The concierge especailly went out of their way to help with directions, bus routes, and taxi cabs. The food in the Pikake Terrace was very good (don't go the buffet, order off the a la carte menu). Room was a good size, clean, and the lanai was perfect to relaxing after a long day of sight- seeing. Only wish that the pool were open later! Do your own research before you go for booking tours to attractions. The travel desk is helpful but their resources are limited to tours that they make comission on selling to you. There are many other tour companies that are cheaper that you can book online on your own. Overall great hotel and would go back in a heart beat!!

<Author>shivos
<Content>We would recommend this hotel!! My wife an I spent a 6 nights at this lovely hotel. After reading some of the prior reviews we were not expecting to be awed by the hotel. We were pleasantly surprised!! The hotel itself was pleasant and well maintained. The hotel room was exactly what we expected too, nothing too fancy but a very reasonably priced place to rest( and a very pretty view from the balcony).The hotel staff was very insightful and helpful. We took advantage of the on site travel/activity coordinator. We obtained wonderful info from this person regarding rental car, luau's, snorkeling.Having gone to this hotel during prime time summer vacation, we were expecting to not find any lounge chairs at the pool. We were again pleasantly surprised, not once did we have any problems finding two seats next to each other. Although it was extremely busy/crowded in town, we did not feel the hotel was overbooked or crowded. Some MAJOR points to note: The hotel offers a hospitality guest room. Basically if your airline happens to fly out late on the day you check out, the hotel offers a complimentary room for you to shower/rest before you head off to the airport. We found this to be invaluable! And all you have to do is ask!If you happen to go to this hotel and are looking for more than just a convenience store(ABC store). There is a Food Pantry grocery store located one major street east of the hotel (2370 Kuhio Ave). We happened to stumble upon it after our 3rd day. The prices are much better at this store for things like snacks, bottled water beer, soda, candy, ice cream. It is a full functioning grocery store. Overall we would return to this hotel. The hotel was in great shape, the staff was wonderful, it is right across the street from the beach(3 minute walk). What more could you ask for.

<Author>Alan_Joanna
<Content>Great location for the money Stayed at the Sheraton PK for 7 nights from 18 June 2008. We were in the high tower initially on the 8th floor but upgraded to a higher floor to get a better ocean view. Room was spacious and had a shower and bath in the bathroom.Didn't eat at the hotel as there are lots of options within walking distance. There is a Denny's if you turn left out of the hotel main entrance and then turn left at the next major street and walk around 200 yards it is on your left. Also there is a cafe if you turn left out of the hotel (on the way to Denny鈥檚) as your approach the man street which does a simple breakfast for $3.95.For dinner we highly recommend the Cheesecake Factory (we ate there twice). The portions are huge and the prices low, especially when you consider you are in Hawaii. Also doing great food is Dukes. We also ate at Nobu as it was our first wedding anniversary. This was pricey (total $240) but worth it for that special meal. Also worth mentioning is PF Changs which is a chain of Chinese restaurants. This was good food and was very cheap too. In terms of tours we did the royal circle island tour which is a full day visiting various sites on ohau including the north shore, pineapple plantation (BTW! the pineapple in Hawaii is the best you will ever taste), look out point from where you can see a large part of the island and a fantastic coconut shrimp place for lunch. Well worth the time and money.We also went to Paradise Cove Luau which was $75 each which sounds a lot for dinner, show and a couple of drinks coupons but it was worth it. If you want to do a luau and get better value you could go to the Polynesian Cultural Centre which also has a series of seven villages that you can see shows and make crafts. The Luau is in the evening. I think the cost of this was $125 but we were put off by the length of the tour 10am and back at 10pm.Waikiki is a really good place and the beach was only a couple of minutes from the hotel. We chose to go to the beach to the left of the hotel and walk about five minutes down the road. It is much less crowded. There is also a Subway, Burger King, McDonalds and an ABC convenience store right across from the beach where we spent our time so it was easy to get something to eat for lunch. The sea was lovely and warm too.To sum up, the Sheraton PK is a mid range hotel in the middle of Waikiki, we were very happy with it and knew it wasn't a five star hotel. We found the staff very helpful and friendly and would stay there again.  
<Date>Jul 14, 2008

<Author>Flyerman
<Content>Good Experience at PK The staff did everything I could have asked for, We wanted a non-smoking room, and at check-in, the man put us on the 7th floor of the smaller building (facing the pool)- the whole floor was non-smoking. It was very clean and fit our needs well for 8 nights. Almost everyday, there were activities in the lobby such as making flower leis,quilting,pineapple cutting, that gave it a sense it was a family atmosphere. Its not a glamorous hotel, but it allows families to experience Hawaii that may not be able to stay in more expensive hotels. The location is great to the beach, and is central to the area activities. The food is expensive-we did not eat there. The one thing I didnt care for was the pool closes at 6:30 pm for the outdoor entertainment but heard many hotel pools close early. There was no fitness center but it looked like they were remodeling one. Aside from these minor issues, I was completely satisfied with the lodging this hotel provided. Would not hesitate to stay there again.

<Author>MakeYouHumble!
<Content>Great hotel We stayed here for our first 2 nights in Hawaii after a long flight from New York. The tower is a great location - not on the beach, but if you're only here for a short stay, you probably won't spend too much time on crowded Waikiki Beach anyway. And if the beach is your thing, it's only a block away. We stayed on the 27th floor - get a high floor if you can. The views are spectacular from the balcony. The staff is friendly - easy check in and check out, and the concierge was very helpful in getting dinner reservations at local restaurants for us. This hotel met all expectations, and even exceeded others with how good the breakfest buffet was. I don't think I'd ever spend a significant amount of time in Honolulu - the north side of Oahu and the other islands are really what Hawaii is all about. But for a short stay after a long flight, this hotel is awesome.

<Author>Kmalia
<Content>Quite Basic We had a corporate rate which was $109/night for a double-occupancy non-smoking room facing the pool (room 710). This building is the shorter tower which runs parallel to the ocean.We stayed there for six nights and found the room to be clean and comfortable, but, as many mentioned, there are some issues which may make me decide to stay somewhere else in the future.PROS- Beds very comfortable- Rooms kept very clean- balconies- Very short walk to Waikiki Beach (2 minutes) and the Waikiki 'strip'- Pool area looked nice- Nice Hawaiian music poolside nightlyCONS- NO valet! upon check-in we pulled up to the curb and a tour bus pulled in behind us, the single 'bell boy' rushed to the tour bus and didn't even look at us - we had to unload our bags ourselves and I had to go park my car in a multi-storey parking garage next door which was ALWAYS packed with cars and had no elevator! Plus - i had to pay $20 a day!- Understaffed - not only the lack of valet, but the front-desk staff seemed overworked, the concierge was almost never there or was inundated with Japanese tourists. I was even told on two occasions, we're short on staff right now- THIN WALLS - we could hear our neighbors conversations through the vents.- Noisy at times - Waikiki Blvd. gets noisy on any day of the week, especially at peak tourist times. if you are an early sleeper (before 9:30pm) the live music down by the pool is very audible every night!All-in-all, i think we got a great rate, but I would probably pay an extra $20-30/night and stay at the Kaimana Beach hotel which is right on the beach and has very friendly and personable staff and a proper valet!

<Author>Kaimanas_Mom
<Content>Good Value We picked the PK as part of our vacation package and the price was reasonable. We stayed in the north tower and could see the Royal Hawaiian hotel from our lanai and a bit of an ocean view. The room was very basic - two queen beds, one chair and a desk with the TV. We were a bit crowded because we also had my 19 month old son's travel playpen with us that was set up between the slider to the lanai and the bed. The furniture itself is old, outdated and in need of replacing. The beds, however, were very nice. Upgraded linens and very comfortable.We did not eat at any of the hotel restaurants because it was kind of pricey. We did sit out and listen to the entertainment by the pool one night and have a few drinks. Nice atmosphere. Can't beat the weather in May.The tower we stayed in only offered dial-up internet connection and it was spotty. The in-room safes did say there was a daily charge for use, but we called the front desk to ask because literature in the room said the safes were available free of charge. The front desk said they don't charge anymore, it's an old sign, but we double checked at the end of our stay and there wasn't a charge, so we were pleased.Other than that, the hotel was perfect for our stay and met our expectations. The location, of course, is beautiful and exactly how mentioned in many of the reviews here. We had no problems here and would stay again!

<Author>purpleturtleuk
<Content>Totally Recommended!!!!!!!! My Family and I stayed here for 15 nights without any problem what so ever and 15 nights is quite a long time!!... I chose the cheapest website with the cheapest rate, upon arrival we were upgraded several times to a room with a pool view (nice in the evening with every night a hula band by the pool) The hotel is a little tired looking in parts but not the communal areas...i get the feeling if your not happy about something, they will attempt to do something about it like moving you're room. The pool area is immaculate and will give you towels to take to the beach... Which is just a 2/3 minute walk away, Its also close to bus stops, shops, car rentals in fact anything you could really need... I had one lunch time snack around the pool which was ok, didn't eat much there though.The room was cleaned very well every day and all the staff seemed fine... I dont know how anyone can hate this place, for the money some places charge in waikiki, this is a bargain... In simple terms, this is a better hotel than the price suggests... I would stay here again no problem... In fact i probably will...

<Author>KitKatChunk
<Content>Good stay; would recommend. We stayed a week from Apr. 11 - 18th and enjoyed the hotel because:1) Great location - heart of Waikiki and close to shops, eateries and car rentals and tour pick-ups. The beach is a few minutes away and just across the street. Also close to bus services.2) Rooms were clean and a good size. We stayed in a high ocean view room (on the side which does not face the pool where there is nightly entertainment and hence may be noisier). Our ocean view was limited however, as there were so many high rises on the beach front which stood in the way. 3) Free pineapple between 2 and 3 pm and if your plane is late, there is a hospital room which you can use for an hour (after you've checked out). Allows you to shower and clean up before hopping on the plane.4) There are free computers (about 4 working stations). The key is to go really late at night or in the middle of the day when most people are out. I think you could also hook up your own laptop if you decide to bring one along.We would stay there again for sure.

<Author>bigjim10
<Content>Not what I have come to expect from Sheraton I guess I might of had higher expectations than I should have to begin with. The hotel is in a fine location (although not right on the beach, it is walking distance to a lot of shopping and eating), the lobby was nice...but that was it. I got there pretty late, so I was tired and hungry - sorry room service ends at 9pm. Mini-bar with snacks? Nope. Vending machine? Nope. Try the ABC market across the street. It was a little irritating that one HAS to leave to hotel for a snack after 9pm. Okay - I get off the elevator and the first thing I see is the Starwood Preferred Guest Floor sign, I immediately think that this actually means something...wrong again. The floor was filthy as were the walls in the hall way. I got to my room and it had a balcony - staring at 4 other buildings/hotels. I do realize that I didn't book an ocean view room - but I guess I expected that the city view room would have a view of the city - and not be 25 feet away from the hotel next door. After getting in bed - I think I realized that the best part of this short three day business trip to Honolulu would be the comfy bed. Although I didn't hear it the first night, on the second and third nights, the faucet in the bath tub dripped all night long. The last morning I decided to go down stairs to try the breakfast buffet. I was okay - nothing spectacular - but acceptable. I ate and proceeded to the check out counter - because I was tired of waiting around for the waitress to take my check - what a mistake that was. The cashier was sooo mean. Everyone that approached her got their heads bitten off...you are better off waiting for the waitress.To wrap up - The PK Hotel wasn't the worst hotel I have stayed at, but I definitely left feeling dissapointed after so many wonderful experiences at Starwood hotels.Side note: I think that was my first and last time to Honolulu. Not because of the Sheraton PK - but because Honolulu has got to be the worst place in Hawaii. I have been to Maui and the Big Island several times each, and I guess I was just spoiled by their natural beauty and lack of sooooo many people and traffic.

The wallpaper was coming loose from the wall in many places, if you looked where the floor met the walls, there was dirt and waste and the bathroom tile floor was a mess, grout was all dirty and corners dirty, the toliet was sitting on the floor at a angle and when you sat on it you thought that you had to hold on so you didnt fall off, There are no dressers just a small set of drawers not enough for one person in the closet, also in the closet was 2 bottles of water with the ice bucket the bottles had a sign on them only $4.25 each comeon high priced room and you have to pay $4.25 for a dollar bottle of water?? Your morning coffee isnt free either in the room, our coffee maker was screwed up open the lid to pour the water in and the hinges were broke so you had the lid in your hand, after the coffee was made there was no way you could remove the pot without opening the filter basket and the same trying to put the pot away. The mattresses have seen there better day and thought that I was going to fall out of bed several times the center is higher then the sides,. Unfriendly very unfriendly staff EXCEPT for the maids and bells very nice people, we went back to the room one day to put some purchases away and the maid was in the room. We told her what we wanted to do and she stopped her work moved the vacuum out in the hallway asked for our room key and shut the door and then used our key to open it, you dont find that at many hotels!!!!! Maid was very security minded. Now the good parts Location Location Location and when we upgraded it was called a ocean view room which it kind of was, you could see the ocean if you stood at the lanai railing but not if you sat in the chairs and the sun set between two hotels and it was very nice. Every day between 2 and 3 they give away free slices of pineapple in the lobby and they have 5 computers with internet that you can use for free. Have to wait your turn and sometimes that was 30 or 40 minutes. So for our 6th trip you can bet we wont be staying at the SPK I could write more but dont want to take up your time as I think you get the point, IT'S NOT WORTH THE MONEY!!!!!!!!

<Author>rachellemb
<Content>We enjoyed our stay My husband and I and 2 kids 6 and 8 stayed here Jan. 2008. We were scared considering some of the reviews, but we really enjoyed our stay. The rooms were dated, and a little rough around the edges, but overall our room was very pleasent and clean. The room had a late 1980s feel. The staff was genuinely friendly and helpful. I can see how where you are located can affect your stay. We were in the Princess tower and our room overlooked the pool and the Westin Moana across the street. It was nice. There is pool entertainment noise at night, but we were so exhausted at night, it didn't bother us. Try to avoid street rooms at the lower levels due to bus noise. This is not a hotel for you if you if you are finicky about your room, or you like to spend a lot of time at your hotel, lounging at the pool, lingering over room service meals, and relaxing. This is not the place for honeymooners. The hotel has a small pool and a busy atmosphere and the rooms are for showering and sleeping. I personally found the atmosphere festive with a I'm on vacation! feel. We are active travelers, who are gone all day, and the room was perfect for us. The beds are comfortable. I like the small Hawaiian touches the hotel provides. Flowers for you hair at the desk, which my daughter loved, pineapple slices and juice in the afternoon, lei making and hula lessons and craft sellers in the lobby and Hawaiian entertainment at night. Though sometimes the night entertainment was very lounge lizardy. We had a discount for the morning buffet that we used. It was very good, with a wide variety of breakfast foods. Our price with the discount made it reasonable, but if your on a budget I would skip it. Avoid the waxy doughnuts, not worth the calories. Yes the name says Sheraton, but with a room rate of about $150 - 200 in expensive Waikiki, you should know that you are not going to get a top notch room and you won't. When they do rehab it, prices will go up accordingly. I felt our room rate was fair for what we got, a clean, comfortable room in a great location.  A hint for those parking with luggage, go to the top part of the parking garage that is labeled additional parking. There is an elevator there that can take you to the lobby. The lower levels do not have an elevator and you have to lug your luggage down stairs. We had a great time in Waikiki, which I usually avoid for the North Shore, and I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>meribor2
<Content>First trip to Hawaii My partner and I went to Hawaii to visit his son who is stationed at Kaneohe Bay, and stayed at the Sheraton for our visit.The bellmen were among the best I've ever encountered - very friendly, very knowledgeable, and quite helpful in getting us oriented. The check in was quick and professional, so no complaints about that part of the process.We stayed in room 236, a king room at the end of the hall with a lanai overlooking the pool, and just immediately over the reception area. While the lanai sliding doors did a pretty credible job of blocking out the noise, if they were open to allow in the lovely breeze, it was VERY noisy. It seemed that there was a tour bus loading up every morning and it was a constant cacophony. The hotel is one block off Kalakaua Blvd, the main drag in Waikiki, so lots of road noise, and at night, lots of noise coming from the street performers as well as the nightly poolside show. In retrospect, I probably should've asked to stay on a higher floor, and perhaps some of it might have been filtered out.The bed was comfortable, the bathroom pretty standardly sized with a pocket door for privacy. We were pretty exhausted the day we arrived from the long flight there, so I didn't notice it immediately, but when I went out onto the lanai the next morning to enjoy some fresh pineapple juice, I noticed a large crack in one of the sliding glass doors, and several bloodstains on the curtains. Now, to their credit, once I pointed it out to the housekeeper, they immediately got to work on it and the front desk called up and offered to move us to a different room, but my partner was ill and uninterested in repacking just to unpack again, so we declined. But it did make me wonder how long it had been there and how often they inspected such things.It seems to be a global trend for hotels to nickel and dime you to death for amenities that should come with the room, which annoys the ever-loving daylights out of me. You have to mount an exploration to find the free channels ( I was looking for CNN) on TV; the menu button on the remote leads you directly to all the pay services. Wireless internet access is expensive, and the signal wasn't that great; you could take advantage of the free desktop computers downstairs, but be prepared to wait, as there was always a queue. There was an in-room safe, which has been free everywhere else I've stayed, but I believe they were charging something like $4.95 a day to use it. There is a free computer solely devoted to checking in for flights and printing boarding passes - but it closes at 9:00 pm when the concierge leaves, and if you want to check in for a flight back to the mainland which leaves at say, 10:45 pm the next night, you can forget about doing anything about it until the concierge returns at 7:30.The breakfast buffet, while tasty, was a ridiculous $21.95 per person. We did it once, and for the rest of our stay opted to go across the street to the ABC store and get fresh fruit salads and sodas there for $5.00 per person, which we could eat in our room, free of the annoying gulls who set up shop in the open-air dining area. As soon as a diner would get up from the table, the birds (who had long since lost any fear of humans!) would swoop in to devour any leftovers on the plate. That was just too creepy for me to deal with, personally. The wait staff tried to shoo the birds constantly, but were overwhelmed by their number and their tenacity.Waikiki Beach is across the street. There are two public beach access points convenient to the hotel; go left (towards the Duke statue and the Police Station), and there's a little snack bar, restrooms, surfboard rentals, etc; there is another if you cross the street at the Moana Surfrider and head up the street towards the Cheesecake Factory. You can check out beach towels poolside with your room key and take them to the beach and then sign them back in when you return.There are several shuttles that pick up across the street - the pink line will take you to Ala Moana Mall for $2 each way; there's also a free Hilo Hattie's shuttle which will take you to their flagship store on Nimitz Blvd. After you've dropped some bucks for the quintessential touristy souvenirs, the shuttle driver will, on request, drop you off at Ala Moana Mall, the Aloha Tower, or the Ward shopping center.The one thing I really liked about the hotel was at 2:15 every day, you could taste fresh pineapple or drink a cup (or two!) of fresh pineapple juice. It was wonderful, and can't recommend it highly enough.

<Author>AshVee
<Content>Great price for a Sheraton hotel close to the beach This was my second time to Waikiki in 2007.The first time I stayed at the Waikiki Marriott where I had my honeymoon. We had a great room but it was pretty expensive.This time I took my mother and decided to stay at the Sheraton Princess K or as I remembered it the Sheraton with the hookers out the front as it was more centrally located (so easier for an older person with mobility issues), much cheaper (USD $185 per night) and was pretty well reviewed on this site. As it was apart of the Sheraton chain I figured it would have to be pretty decent too. This hotel is good value for money especially when you compare it to a lot of the other hotels that are pretty much in exactly the location. We stayed around Thanksgiving and I was surprised at how cheap it was considering it was a peak holiday time in the USA and there were plenty of guests. It is a short stroll to the beach and surrounded by good shops, restaurants and close to the Food Pantry supermarket on Kuhio Avenue.The lobby and pool area is great and I was pleasantly surprised with our room on the 29th floor. It wasn't the Marriott and as others have commented, the hotel could do with a refurbishment soon. The beds and bedding were wonderfully comfortable and the room was clean and in good condition with a good size lanai. That said the bathroom reminded me of the shower scene in Psycho (very 1950's) and after a few days there seemed to be a bit of mould near the top of the shower rail that was mysteriously never cleaned by housekeeping. The room faced the International Marketplace (not the ocean like it was supposed to but you could technically see the ocean) so it was pretty noisy until midnight and I had to sleep with earplugs a couple of nights. We didn't eat at the hotel as it was expensive and there were so many great restaurants within a short walking distance. The free Overall it was good and I would stay here again and recommend it as a mid range accommodation. I have stayed in much worse places than this!!!! Some of the hotels off Kuhio Avenue looked pretty rubbish in comparison so I think the Princess K is pretty good considering that hotels tend to be pretty expensive in Waikiki. Most importantly, the whole point of going on holiday is not to stay in your room! Get out and experience what you came to Hawaii for!

<Author>tlynch19
<Content>Overall, a very good vallue We stayed at the PK (as the locals call it) from December 10-15th and were generally happy with this hotel. Was it a five star experience? No. But the price was right and the location was great - right accross the street from the beach front hotels (which cost way more). We payed a bit extra to get a room with a high ocean view and were pleased with the view from our lanai. Waikiki is an urban area: there are homeless people, street performers and prostitutes. That's part of the deal. If you want to avoid this, go to Maui. Yes, the hotel buffet was expensive, but this is Hawaii people; everything is expensive! The nice thing about Waikiki compared to some of the quieter islands is that there are so many food options within walking distance you don't have to limit yourself to expensive hotel food. Overall, I would say this hotel was a good value and very well situated.

<Author>Drdonuttail
<Content>Good location, not for resort seekers Overall, for the price, this was a good place to stay. The central location was great with the beach just across the street. Lots of restaurants and shops were adjacent and the short blocks made walking around town quite easy. The public bus and paid trolley stops were nearby. Bus/organized tours picked up right outside the hotel.The pool was only open from 9am-6pm and there was no hot tub to warm up in after swimming at the beach. The hotel itself didn't have a gym, though the sister Sheraton hotel had facilities where you could pay to get in, if you wished. There were some restaurants at the hotel which we did not visit (there are so many around that were less expensive). At 2pm, the hotel offered pineapple carving where you could help yourself to fresh pineapple juice and pineapple slices (delicious) even if you're not a guest, you could stroll in and induldge!. During the day, there were a few vendors selling crafts by the pool.The rooms were small, but very clean. I loved the pillows though I found the mattress a little firm. Our view towards the west wasn't much. Unfortunately, we were located on the 3rd floor which TOTALLY SUCKED BECAUSE IT WAS REALLY NOISY FROM 4AM unti 11PM. The people traffic wasn't bad - the problem was that shuttle buses and tour buses would idle outside on the street picking up passengers. Very annoying. We did ask for a room overlooking the poolside when we checked in, but apparently, they didn't have anything available. Because we wanted two adjacent rooms, we elected to stay where we were. Although some rooms had connecting doors, ours didn't so I guess that we should have requested new rooms on the second day. Oh bother!Hotel summary: good location, clean rooms, nice staff, and good price BUT request rooms towards the poolside and remember that this is not a resort hotel - there's so much to see in Oahu - don't plan to spend much time at the hotel. Go experience Hawaii!Recommended outings: Germaine's luau, Giovanni's shrimp truck, Duck tour - Pearl Harbor, Hanauma Bay, Kailua kayaking, Diamond Head, Happy Trails horseback riding, Waimea Audobon Center (waterfall!), Waikiki Aquarium, Makani Catamaran

<Author>tpleck
<Content>Not Sure I can Add Much to what has been already said. Well, I am not sure I can really add much to what has been already said about the hotel. I was alittle surprised by how small the room was. One of the cabinets is taken up for the frig and the safe, so you were left with very little space to unpack. There are drawers in the closet, but they are quite small. I guess it just was hard to keep the room very tighty with so little storage space. We did have to deal with the noise, but I was so worn out each night, I really did not have any trouble sleeping. What I would really want you to know is, if you are looking for a resort type enviroment, this is not the place for you. It is a hotel and no more. They try by having bands by the pool and bring in vendors to sell hats, jewelry, etc. They also have a few classes such as lei making, but they are in the middle of the day and most people are already out and about. The location is great if you are looking for shopping and yes there does seem to be an ABC Store on every block! The beach is not far and the hotel is great about letting you take their towels from the pool area to the beach. As a Starwood Preferred guest we are suppose to get late check out, when I went to the front desk the day before we left, I was told they were totalled booked and would not get late check out. I called the next morning and was told no problem. This really helped as our flight did not leave until late that night so we were able to visit the beach one last time and really enjoy our last day in Hawaii. I visited with one of the clerks at the Thor store and she told me that Honolulu is not what Hawaii is about, you really need to visit the other islands to get the true aloha spirit. We did take a one day trip to Maui and really enjoyed it. The only down side is the hurry up and wait at the airport. We had to wait over an hour and a half each way at the airport. So, if you are going to shopping, spend alittle time at the beach and site see this hotel will work for you. If you are looking for a laid back, romantic holiday, keeping looking!

<Author>freebyrd97
<Content>So-so accommodations This hotel is below what I'd consider 3 stars for a US hotel. I've been in 3 star hotels in Mexico that were nicer and better equipped than the Princess Kaiulani. The staff are all very nice, but the room was fairly cruddy - all the bathrooms were very old with floors that had very questionable, moldy looking stains in the grout and it was very cramped - if one person is standing up in the room, you'd get claustraphobic just looking in from the doorway. I had to sleep in a room where water dripped from the ceiling onto my head for 2 nights before they felt it was appropriate to move me. The hotel is very conveniently located right across the street from the beach, next to the International Marketplace, but I was almost embarrassed to tell people where I was staying. Bottom line - good location explains the rates, but overall, it's a rundown hotel that you wouldn't expect to find in the hotel zone right along Kalakaua Avenue next to all the expensive, high end retail shops.

<Content>Location, Location, Location My husband and I travelled to Hawaii to celebrate our first wedding anniversary. Close to the shops, beach, restuarants. I see what people mean when they compare it to other Sheratons. However, it's good value for money and would suit those who would rather spend their money exploring the island that on a glitzy hotel. Hire a car, go on a submarine trip, climb diamond head. It's a paradise island, and for us was a trip of a lifetime.

<Author>Puchalski
<Content>Much Better than Expected The SPK actually was a nice hotel. I had low expectations based on the prior reviews and the cheap price I paid.I booked the cheapest room on the Sheraton website and was upgraded to a partial oceanview on the 23rd floor overlooking the international market. Once the drummers stopped playing around 11pm, the room became very quiet.Check-in was fast, friendly and efficient. All of the staff were very friendly and helpful. The lobby nicer than I expected, very open with a nice breeze. Elevators were a little slow and always packed.We asked the concierge about a nice simple seafood restaurant that wasn't overly expensive and she gave us a few recommendations, none of which were in any of the local Starwood hotels. I'm glad she can give out recommendations that don't include their hotels. We ate at Ocean House and it was great.The pool was nice and not overly crowded. Plenty of towels too.The pool bar wasn't overly exciting, so I went over to the Westin for drinks which was the best place go for happy hour.The breakfast buffet was overpriced at $22. We ate at Duke's instead for $15 and got an ocean view.The location was perfect. The beach was across the street. Tons of restaurants and bars very close the hotel. Hertz car rental was across the street too.The only problem we had with the hotel, was that I was supposed to have champagne and a cheese plate in my room when I arrived and it wasn't there. They delivered it much later, which ruined the whole point of having it.Overall, I would definitely stay there again for $125 a night.

<Author>smlworldtraveler
<Content>Decent hotel, great location The hotel is right across from the Moana Surfrider and Waikiki beach. You can't check in until after 3pm and there is no valet parking. You have to park your car around the corner at the parking garage located behind the hotel, cost is $15 per day. Make sure you get your parking validation ticket as soon as you check in! We didn't know about that and had to pay $9 for parking our car in the garage for 3 hours and it was the lady at the parking garage who told us about the valdiation slip. We had asked for a Deluxe Ocean View and got a room at the top floor (11th) with an awesome view of the ocean. They have live entertainment around the pool area from about 7pm to 9:30pm and if you stay in the wing facing Waikiki beach and Kalakua road, you could enjoy the entertainment from your balcony with some snacks. Our room was very spacious with two ceilign fans to keep you cool and the Air conditioner on low to save energy. The bathroom was a little small and on our first night there was a littel trouble with the hot water, some yellowish water was coming out. But I think that was because we were in the old wing and it took the pipes a while to work. The next morning all was well and the hot water was spewing out clear water. The water pressure on the shower was good.There are plenty of ABC stores around you. International Market is like a two minute walk from the pool area and the Royal Hawaiian center was right across the street. This hotel has a great location and is not as heavily priced as the other Sheraton hotels around Waikiki.

<Author>Toadman
<Content>Not a bad hotel Just returned from a memorial weekend trip to Ohau. We had a five night stay and overall had no major complaints. The lower floors can get street noise if you are facing the street, which we were. We were on the fourth floor Kaiulani Wing. This faces the King Shops. The pool as are all the pools that we saw along the hotels in Waikiki is rather small for the size of this hotel but when you have such a great beach right across the street who wants a pool?We used the safe on a few occassions and were not charged for it at check-out. It's says on the safe that they charge $3.50/day. The large lanai was nice. There was an empty fridge in the room, which we filled with water/drinks from the ABC store. Our room was right above the parking area for the tour buses so we were awoken each morning to the sound of diesel bus enigines. The hotel is showing its age. The elevators in our wing broke one day while we were there and I had a steel tube from the sink drop on to my foot, causing a large cut that bled profusely. The hotel staff is friendly and overall the value and location of this hotel makes it a good deal for people looking for a decent and clean place to stay on Waikiki with out paying the higher prices for the location. We'd stay hear again.

<Author>sazer1
<Content>Location, Location,and, well, not much else. If your idea of a hotel in paradise is a business, group/convention oriented, fast-paced hotel that is tired, run down and in great need of renovations, stay here. Otherwise, do the right thing and choose another Starwood property. The only reason to stay here is because you can't afford the rates or the points for a better property (i.e. Royal Hawaiian, Moana, Sheraton Waikiki or W). My partner described the noise level of this hotel as 'metropolis.' I have stayed in much quieter hotels in downtown Manhattan. All night we heard trash trucks and sirens and traffic and harleys. I think the issue is that the hotel has no sound insulation at all. Many street performers gather in front of the hotel area at night, and they can bang on drums until late into the evening which will keep the entire hotel awake. The elevators are painfully slow and small. The rooms are old and tired. They don't have Sheraton sweet sleaper beds here, and they do very little in my opinion to cater to Starwood Platinum members here, including a marginal upgrade and not allowing a late checkout. Every other hotel we went to made this place seem like a Best Western. When you call to complain (i.e., the maid never brought more towels an hour after calling the service promise desk), they really don't seem to care much. The hotel lobby itself always seems to smell like raw fish and moldy carpet. I was embarrassed I booked this hotel and encourage you to look elsewhere unless you are OK with 3-star standards and a lot of noise. This is not the Hawaii you see on the postcards...

<Author>cicitrvlr
<Content>Mixed review - the good the bad the ugly I need to caveat this by explaining that I live in a hotel 300 days per year, and I am kind of a hotel snob. This Sheraton was ok - definitely not the type of Sheraton I am used to - i.e. no sweet sleeper bed (bed was uncomfortable, pillows were lumpy and the comforter was a scratchy, thin spread popular with motels), no soft towels, not renovated - but it was clean, simple and a good value. I actually stayed there on Starwood Points and it was only 7,000 points per night - not bad since the other Sheratons nearby were 12,000 per night and up. The staff was friendly, the location was good (right next to a ABC store, a few restaurants, and the International Marketplace) and I rented a car so I could escape Waikiki when the tourists got overwhelming. There were a lot of tour groups and school trips there, which got a little tiresome (MUST you scream to your friends down the hallway at 3am??) but overall - good value for the price, and it doesn't promise a 5 star experience, so I knew what I was in for.

<Author>mxtang
<Content>Excellent Location, Great Value!! We were very pleased with our hotel stay here. The location can't be beat. Waikiki is the best place within Oahu to stay in. Everything is so close and convenient. Buses run everywhere.First off the location of this hotel was great because: we were among the first people to get off the shuttle from the airport and last people to be picked up. Nothing worst than taking a shuttle and be last to be dropped off or first to be picked up. If you have a car rental or can take a taxi then great for you but I'm sure most people would like to save where they can. Bad thing about car rental is that you have to pay for parking which can be expensive!Check in and out was quick. Wasn't a long line at all. People weren't bubbly but friendly. They had free internet access downstairs and 3 different FREE newspapers! SWEET!!Our room was on the eighth floor. Room was fairly small, not that much longer than the bed but they did have a full size mirror which made it longer and a nice balcony. AC was a bit noisy, not horrible but definitely not one of your quiet newer models. We didn't lose any sleep due to that though.Room was clean and fairly well kept. Our tub's drainage was a bit slow though. I find that's an issue in quite a few hotels.The concierge were helpful. The buffet they offered was a bit expensive. I wouldn't recommend unless it's a Friday when they offer lobster and steak for $3 more than normal. That would be a great value but we didn't stay there long enough for that.Beach, shopping, food all nearby. Don't try the local food places. They are either small in size or lacking in quality. If you see a small price, know what you're getting. I would stay with the more established and well known. We love Denny's for breakfast. You can take the bus to almost everywhere but make sure you know when they start running for certain lines.

<Author>Canadiantravels
<Content>Great price for the location We stayed in Honolulu for one night in February. Since it was just a one night stay before heading back home, we weren't looking for an expensive hotel. Most of the hotels in Honolulu seemed to be older so we weren't expecting too much. The hotel is situated at a great location - just across from the beach (but not on the beach itself). But it does have a very nice swimming pool and is relatively less crowded than Wikiki beach on a nice day. From the airport, you can take a shuttle to the hotel for US$9 per person (contact the hotel to arrange a pick up time) or a taxi wlll cost about US$40 depending on traffic. There are lots of restauants and shops just along the strip so you won't have a problem finding places to go. The only negative about the hotel is that they have a live band who plays at night till about 9:30 or 10pm, which can be heard on the floors above (we were on the 22nd floor), but you can request a room on the other side of building if you wanted a quieter room. A great price (US$144) for the location if you're not looking for anything fancy.

<Author>cookmonger
<Content>No Complaints Here We were scared off by the reviews, but wanted to try it because of its value. Surprisingly the hotel is very nice, 3-star hotel. Obviously there were some room for improvements (the carpet was old, the hallways were old as well), but the room was manageable (it was a little small, but since we weren't there much except to sleep, it made no difference to us). The location is extremely convenient. It's across the street from the ABC store, as well as the King Street Shopping. There were plenty of things to keep you entertained at the hotel (live band nightly by the pool, and music going on 'til 11 pm most weekends). It's about a block and a half from Waikiki Beach, so the location is just top notch, without having to pay too much for it. We were located on the 4th floor, with views of the street (no pool view, no ocean view), and it was fine. I think there were other reviews complaining of the noise/music, but when you're in Hawaii, nothing less should be expected than some occasional street performers, and people walking late at night. Besides, the shops are open late (usually 11pm or later), so it's expected to hear the cabs, cars, and pedestrians mingling about.All in all, if on a budget (~$150 or less per night), this is the perfect choice.

<Author>jetset007
<Content>Not the Typical Sheraton As a Starwood Gold Member, I received a 35% off offer in the mail from SPG. I made a reservation for 9 days at the Princess Kaiulani at a rate of $153 per night. I requested an upgrade to the Ainahua tower via email and phone calls directly to the hotel. Upon arrival, I was upgraded to the Princess Tower - which is NOT your typical Sheraton room (old furniture, carpet and small bathroom  tub with old fixtures). The only positive comment about Room 536 was that it was a corner room with a nice lanai facing the beach. Unfortunately, the room did NOT offer the Sheraton Sweet Sleeper bed, even though the website references same. I learned the lesser of all towers is the Kaiulani Tower - I would NEVER have stayed in that old tower. Apparently, I was upgraded from the Kaiulani tower to the Princess tower (2 upgrades) as a SPG gold member; however, I was not impressed. After the third day, I was finally upgraded to the Ainahua Tower (as originally requested) to Room 2856 - with an awesome view of Waikiki Beach. This tower and room is more like the Sheraton you are accustomed. Definitely avoid the other two towers. Unfortunately, the front desk will not inform you as to which tower until check in; or you may call late the morning of arrival to determine same. Otherwise, the entire staff was friendly and accommodating. The negative reviews about this hotel are apparently comments from guests who had rooms in the older two towers. Again, not your typical Sheraton. Also, the pool is adjacent to the lobby, restaurant/bar area with live nightly entertainment and lots of tourists - thus, no privacy or quiet pool area. Aloha!

<Author>patinseatt
<Content>GO while you still can Location, location, location. That about sums up the true strong point of this hotel. Magnificently located just steps from the beach this hotel offers a center of everything location in Waikiki. Travelling with a friend, we were fortunate to get a room in the newer, tallest building in the 3 tower hotel complex. Our room, on the 29th floor, had a spectacular view of the ocean. The room itself was fair-sized and well kept with a terrific balcony overlooking the beach. The hotel itself looks a bit tired and we have since learned that the other 2 towers are scheduled to be torn down and replaced with condos, while the building we stayed in will be closed, renovated, and reopened as a more luxurious property.Even though this in not the Ritz, I heartily recommend staying here while you can, since at the rate we paid (less than 50% of the rate for a similar room at the nearby, bigger Sheraton hotel) is, all things considered, an absolute bargain. GO while you can and enjoy Waikiki while there is still an affordable quality hotel there. Soon they'll all be replaced by much more expensive luxury properties.

<Author>JuzzyBear
<Content>Sydney, Australia We have stayed in Waikiki several times but this is the 1st time at the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani, we arrived at 10.30am  were greeted by friendly staff  also given a room upgrade to a Ocean View Room on the 24th floor which was ready at this early check in time. My husband  I were in Hawaii celebrating our 10 yr anniversary  was very pleased with the all round appearance of the hotel, very central to all areas of waikiki. We enjoyed the free nightly entertainment. I have read previous reviews about the noise of the area, to those who want peace  quiet go to another Island. The cost of the Buffet was a bit pricey, you can go around the corner to Smorgy for $20 less, or across the road to Dukes Buffet which is directly on the beach, Don't call direct to another Country from your Hotel Room or it will cost you $$. We will be staying here again next year.

<Content>Sheraton Princess was quite nice, after reading all the terrible reviews! We stayed in the newest tower (Ainhau) in a corner High Ocean View, 12th floor. We did not do the breakfast or evening buffets $20-$30 per person, though the presentations were very nice  food smelled delicious. We walked across the street to the Outrigger Hotel  had breakfast at Hula Grill ($7  up) gorgeous ocean view. Dukes at Outrigger had a buffet brkfst. for $12 0r $13 . These are both good  reasonable for all 3 meals. Our room was fine, you could hear the traffic noise below  nightly entertainment, but keep in mind your in downtown Honolulu in the center of Waikiki Beach. The noise didn't interfere with our naps or nightly rest. Our room was a fair size, bathroom clean  functional, a/c kept us cool. This hotel was built in the 50's  60's, so everything isn't perfect, but then our home is only 6yrs. old  it's not PERFECT anymore either. If your a perfectionist, maybe you'd rather pay $100 -$200 or more a night  stay at the Hilton Hawaiin Village where we stayed previously . The Sheraton Princess is in a great location for walking everywhere!! We also walked in the other wings of the hotel, out of curiosity after reading all the horrible reviews, they looked fine from what we saw, balconies may have been somewhat smaller. You can't beat this hotel for the price. PLEASED GUESTS from Atlanta, GA.

<Author>cemden
<Content>The only hotel to stay at in Waikiki Great hotel on Waikiki. I have stayed here in 1983, 1985, 1995, 2005, and now am planning 2 weeks in May 2007. I have read most of the review found of this website, and I find some of them to be very unfair. I have never been disappointed in my room or the hotel. I do not stay at low end hotels. I do not accept the argument that you only spend a few hours in a room, so why pay more. I enjoy a nice, new room, with all the amenities. I have stayed at the Sheraton Surf rider, the Sheraton Waikiki, Hilton Rainbow. I find the Princess Kai to be of equal quality in terms of the rooms, but a better price because it is across the streetEvery morning for 2 weeks, I pick up breakfast at the Princess Kai food court, carry it across the street, and sit in the pool area facing the beach at the Sheraton Moana-Surfrider. I have never been turned away by other Sheraton Hotels staff. I normally spend about 2 hours eating, reading the newspaper or a book, and enjoy the view of Diamond Head. I usually go in low season, and after making reservations online, I check them over and over again. Every time I find a lower price, I change it. In Oct 2005, I paid an average of $123 per night (incl 5th night free offer). Those that complain about the price, are not very good shoppers. I have never seen any part of the hotel in disrepair. The walls are not paper-thin. I paid for a partial ocean view, and recived a great view of Diamond Head, and ocean. I did not have to hang over the balcony rail with some one holding my feet to see the ocean or Diamond Hear. I enjoy the music from the pool area every night. The music is loud, but isn't that why you go to Hawaii?There is no better value on Waikiki Beach. The walk from the lobby to the street to the pool/beach at the Moana-Surfrider is short- less than 3-4 minutes if you have to wait for the traffic light. One of the things I like most about the Princess Kai is that it is not one of those hotel that have 15 min walk to the street. Shop for the price, and enjoy the Princess Kai.

<Content>Don't waste your money We spent 4 days here in August 2006, and wished we had gone elsewhere. Please when booking this hotel don't buy a room that states high escape ocean view. Everything at this hotel seems to be 'EXTRA', if you want to use the gym it costs, the safe in the room costs, parking costs $15 day. But the main factor was the noise. Every night there was karoke or another form of entertainment going on near the hotel and the noise travelled. We were awake until 2 am most nights and as a result got up later the next day. When checking out we were able to leave our bags and use the hotel pool, there was also a room to have a shower in before the flight. I would not stay here again and i would definately not recommend this hotel, there are other hotels which offer a better choice. Do not go for the brand name sheraton as i feel this is not a sheraton hotel with the standards i would expect. i prefered Aqual Palms with a 15 min walk to wakiki centre.

<Author>landh
<Content>Just Awful Luckily we only had to stay here for one night! I really wished I had shower shoes to wear in there! and to make matters worse, our tub was clogged and didn't drain so the hotel plumber was sent up and spent an hour getting the clog half cleared for us! The rest of the room was okay, shabby like I said, but not as attrocious as the bathroom. the one grosser thing, however, about the bed was that our bed was short-sheeted! so there was 2 inches of exposed mattress and mattress pad (again, very old and gross looking). I slept with my feet on top of the top sheet! And of course removed the bed spread completely.At least we had a view, and it was only one night, but I would recommend you avoid this hotel unless you're a group of college kids looking for a lower priced room. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not Sheraton-like We stayed at the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani June 26-July 3rd, 2006 and I wouldn't do it again. The place is worn down and tired with it's carpet from the 80's and small rooms with paper-thin walls. We stayed in the main part of the hotel on the 8th floor ... I guess the 'towers' are newer and a little nicer (or so they claim) but they didn't look much nicer to me. Our travel agent told us that free parking was included, which is typical at the nicer hotels, but we got there to a snooty receptionist that informed us that they charge their guests $10 a day to park in their POS parking garage with no elevators and then they reserve half of the first floor for their employees so ALL guests are walking and most are trekking up and down stairs. The restaurants are nice and you can use any of the neighboring (MUCH nicer) Sheraton hotel restaurants and charge it directly to your room. Sadly enough, they consider this perk one of the great benefits of staying in their hotel. If you get a chance to stay at any of the other three Sheratons on the same block, I highly recommend it. We could hear everything from our neighbor's room ... we heard their afternoon chats, their party and every TV show that they watched. Luckily, we didn't stay in the room much but with 3 different groups in that room while we were there, and none of them overly loud, we heard each one of them so it wasn't just a case of one loud neighbor. The one group that threw the party even invited us over because they knew that the walls were thin and they planned on making some noise ... we declined but appreciated the offer and took a midnight stroll on the beach instead. The best thing you can say about the hotel is that it is centrally located on Waikiki beach. If you get bored, or can't sleep because of all the noise, just step out the front door of the hotel and you are on the main drag and a great touristy-type surfing area with rental boards and all is located right across the street. Some websites, and our travel agent (Our ex-travel agent) rated this as a 4-Star hotel ... that's not even close to the truth. It's a 3-star at best. They claim to be cheaper than the other hotels in that area but that's like comparing apples to oranges. They ARE cheaper than their neighboring competition but that's because they're not as good as the hotels that they're comparing themselves to ... they compare their prices to 5-star hotels across the street ON the beach. If you think you found an awesome hotspot at a great price then keep looking because you'll only be disaapointed. I also found it interesting that the hotel's comment service on their TV didn't work and when I asked for a comment card at the front desk they couldn't seem to find one ... so I wrote my comments on a post-it note and gave it to them. Speaking of which, we voiced our concerns only about items that we felt management would be able to correct, in order to avoid sounding like a whining guest and in return we were treated like a whining guest complete with rolling eyes and deep sighs. Nothing was done ... not a shocker at all. Overall, we had one of the best vacations of our lives but that was no thanks to anything the folks at this hotel provided. We spent very little time in our room, which is a good thing while you're in Hawaii, and we enjoyed ourselves immensely. Go to Hawaii and have a good time, but if you're looking at the Sheraton Princess Kiaulani for a room you might as well save some money by booking a complete dive and avoid the let-down. This place was not very Sheraton-like at all.  
<Date>Jul 6, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>centrally located but other problems prevailed My wife is from Hawaii so we visit at least two to three times a year. Normally we stay at the Outrigger on the beach (right accross the street from the Princeess Kaiulani) and have had absolutely great service.We booked a last minute trip for June 2006 at the Princess Kaiulani and found the experience dissappointing.The main problems:1. Parking has no valet, and the first side of the paring structure has no elevators, so you could end up climbing 5 flights of stairs to get to your car. It wasn't until our second day there that another guest told us to drive to the top of this parking structure and then drive to an adjacent lot that provided access to elevators. It would have been nice if the hotel could have communicated this in the beginning.2. Any item billed to your room is sent for a credit authorization of the original dollar amount times the amount of days you are staying. For example, our parking was $70 so the cc authorization was $70 x 7 days or $490. We had room service the first night for $108, so that authorized $108 x 7 or $ 756. They had tied up over $1200 of our money in two transactions. This is obviously not something they tell you at check-in so be aware.3. The pool was shut down two days due to contamination.4. Small room, small tv, small fridge.5. They charge extra for items we received free at the Outrigger on the Beach i.e. $3 for the safe, bottled water (complamentary at the Outrigger).On the plus side:1. The hotel did make an effort to resolve the credit authorization problem.2. The staff was polite.3. This hotel is centrally located4. The rooms are ok -definately not as nice as the review pictures.We are scheduled to go back to Hawaii in October and had originally booked this Princess Kaiulani hotel. When we had problems I called our travel agent and switched hotels back to the Outrigger on the Beach. I sure we will enjoy our stay much better at the Outrigger.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good value We stayed at the Princess Kaiulani last week (5/4-5/12). The hotel is very centrally located to Waikiki Beach. The area where Waikiki beach is unobstructed by all the oceanfront hotels is less than half a block away. Trust me, if you want to get to the beach and you aren't staying in one of the oceanfront hotels it can be a real chore. It's also centrally located to all kinds of shopping, Coach, Chanel, Dior, and other high end shops are right down the street. The hotel is also right next door to the International Marketplace. This was not so good. Don't be fooled by the name, it is a total tourist trap. It also happens to be the gathering place for a number of street performers, a couple of whom bang on drums until 12-1am in the morning every night. Even on the 16th floor the drums were rather loud and sometimes made it hard to get to sleep. The lobby area was open air and looked out over the pool which was very nice. There were plenty of chairs around the pool and there was also a nice lounge/restaurant area around the pool. The lounge served a $20 breakfast buffet every morning, overpriced for breakfast if you ask me. We went across the street to the Hula Grill for breakfast, it was less expensive, had great food, and a fantastic view of the ocean. They also served dinner buffet style or a la carte. Either way, at $33-35 for the buffet and $17+ for entrees it was also overpriced. If you intend on staying near the hotel for lunch/dinner, I suggest Duke's which is across the street a level below the Hula Grill. Now to the room, for $200/night I expected a little more, but based in comparison pricing for hotel rooms, $200/night doesn't get you much in Hawaii. At $200/night we've stayed in much, much nicer rooms/hotels than this. The room was a little small and the decorating was dated, but all in all it was acceptable. We had a partial ocean view room and the view was spectacular. We got lucky and had a room right on the corner of the hotel closest to the water so I can't guarantee all partial ocean vews are this good, but ours could just as well have been a full ocean view. The maid service wasn't great, they forgot to refill our coffee, replace towels, vaccuum, or take used dishes on different occasions. Other than that the staff was courteous and very helpful with directions, etc. Overall, the hotel was adequate. We got about what we expected and I would say at this price range it's a fairly safe choice.  
<Date>May 17, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved Sheraton We went to Honolulu during the school spring break about two weeks ago. This was our first time visit Hawaii with three small children(7, 4 1). We stayed in Sheraton Princess Kaiulani Hotel and we loved it. We had a one bedroom suite with two double beds on 10th floor with both ocean and city view. The hotel is clean and convenient. The room had a fridge and and sink area with coffee maker. It has cabinet above the sink area for storage and it's a big plus for famiy with infant or toddler to put the bottles, baby food for drinks. The bathroom is large enough to let our whole family staying inside to watch my little one bathing. There is a closet with sliding door which I have not seen before. It's very thoughtful. We tried the hotel's breakfast buffet and everything was fresh made. The kids ate free and you paid for adults only. The eating area is outdoor next to the pool. The only thing I would compliant was the birds would fly or around the eating area. It's little bit annoying but the lovely food and weather could make it up.The location of the hotel is great, you don't need a car at all. International Market Place and Waikiki beach are only few minutes walking away. You can get some less expensive but still delicious Japanese and Korean food in the food court at International Maket Place. We will definitely come back to this hotel next time. We had a good experience and fun time there.I

<Author>gameover
<Content>Great stay and value The only reason I would not rate this as excellent is because it's not on the beach, but across the street is good enough. Location can't be beat, restaurants everywhere, Duke's and Chuck's Steak House across the street and it has a food court next to the pool for early morning coffee and breakfast.
