<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good location and price for waikiki I just returned from Waikiki in April 2006. We stayed at the Prince Kaiulani and had a great time. This is a very clean and reasonably priced hotel for waikiki. The best features are the price, people (very friendly) and the service. The only thing that was not that great was the food (breakfast buffet).Its overpriced and not worth your money. If your looking for a great breakfast at reasonable price, go to the Hula Grill right across the street above Dukes. They have excellent pancakes and the view is unbeatable. Another small downfall is the lack of internet access in your room. They do have a computer room with 4 computers, but you may have to wait a few minutes to use one. Other than that, I would certainly recommend this place for the money if you don't have $300 a night to blow on a room.

<Author>Ryanoles
<Content>Not up to expectations For a Starwood/Sheraton hotel I was rather disappointed by this place.I spend plenty of time before going on vacations researching hotels because I never want to end up with a poor quality one. This hotel was the first one I missed the mark on. Based on location, cost, photographs, and previous reviews I was certain that this hotel would be a good one, but I wasn't that impressed.The staff is very friendly and courteous, which was a plus, but friendly staff doesn't make up for the rock hard mattresses and moldy washrooms. My room was on the 14th floor (Starwood Preferred Guest floor) but was noisy at all hours of the day and night. They have some kind of music playing from about 9:00 pm until some hour of the night (I always was able to somehow fall asleep while it was still blasting) and the sounds of traffic and people are very irritating.I never utilized the pool since it was always packed full of people, so instead of swimming shoulder to shoulder with all the other SPK guests, I opted to spend time elsewhere.The one good thing about this place is the access to all of Waikiki, which is very convienient. It is within walking distance to so many things (Zoo, Kapiolani park, aquarium, Waikiki beaches, restaurants, shops, Internation marketplace, etc.) which really cut back on the taxi fares that I broke my bank on when I stayed at the Hilton Hawaiian Village, which for $40/night more is far superior and recommended by me.I wouldn't return to the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani again if I were to go back to Waikiki, I would rather re-do my research and find another place to stay since I wouldn't think it would be that difficult to find something more satisfactory.

<Author>gerns
<Content>These Kiwi's loved the PK Have just spent 7 nights at the Sheraton PK. Not sure about all wings of accommodation, but we had rooms on 23 and 20 floors. Decor was a little dated, but King beds were so comfortable, rooms very clean, air conditioning units very effective, views amazing and the hotel location was awesome. Housekeeping staff were excellent and very friendly. Front desk staff okay, but the poolside restaurant and bar staff could do with a shake up! We never had problems having to wait on the lifts, the four in our wing worked very efficiently.We live at the beach in NZ and there are no ocean views at night, so really appreciated the views of the ocean during the day and the activity and lights after dark. We did not have any traffic noise at night on 23rd floor.We tried a couple of breakfast venues, but settled on Duke's and Shore Bird as value for money and catering to our tastes. Evening meal choice limitless, but our favourite was Diamond Head Grill in the W hotel, food excellent, service brilliant - good value.This was our 3rd trip to this Island and we will definitely be staying at the Sheraton PK again next time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location....OK Hotel I stayed at the Sheraton PK with my wife and 1 year old daughter for a week in a Ocean View Room on the 24th floor. Being a Sheraton hotel I expected a little nicer place, but I guess a lot of hotels in Waikiki seem a little run down. Not exactly what I expected but the reviews I read had some truths and fallacies about them. I will begin by saying the staff is very friendly and try and accommodate every need. I read a lot of the reviews and decided for the price and location I would go with the PK, if I had to do it again I would stay at the Sheraton Waikiki instead. The hotel is a little dated and the rooms are really bland and the beds are the most uncomfortable beds I have ever experienced at a Sheraton. Clearly this Sheraton is not a part of the Heavenly sleep program. It is a good clean hotel and centrally located to everything, next to the International Market place, across the street from the beach, has a food court next to the pool and right in the middle of bars and restaurants. I visited the other 3 Sheratons and after accessing the amenities and cost I believe the Sheraton Waikiki is the best choice. The Surfrider is a beautiful hotel but not worth the price. The Royal Hawaiian seemed like a pink funhouse...couldn't wait to get out of there and the Sheraton Waikiki seemed it was the best all around for price, amenities and location.

<Author>CindyYZ
<Content>Never again...Go stay at the Sheraton Waikiki I was in Hawaii for my best friend's wedding and stayed at the Sheraton Waikiki for 3 nights and had to move to the Kaiulani for the final night (the Waikiki one was sold out the final night). After spending 3 blissful days at a beautiful hotel with their signature heavenly bed (aahh), I ended up moving over to this dump of a hotel. The price difference was only about $35 a night but it felt like you dropped 3 stars in hotel class.Where to begin.. the hotel seems pretty old and not maintained well. After check in, the elevators are tiny and there's only a few, so the wait is long. My room had a standard foam mattress with the thin mattress cover/blankets you find at cheap motels. The bathroom was extremely tiny with a sliding door and the showerhead and tiles looked incredibly dirty. I really felt grossed out by them. The worst part is, there was a mosquito in my room and after spending 40 minutes (unsuccessfully) swatting at it, I gave up and had to endure this unwelcomed guest. After talking to some other friends that ended up there, I found out that I was actually upgraded due to my starwood status as my room had a small couch and a balcony overlooking the pool. I checked out the standard room and it's even worse. Never again... for the type of money you'll spend going to Hawaii, you want to feel relaxed and comfortable at the hotel. For $35 bucks more, go to the Sheraton Waikiki, I highly recommend that hotel!

<Author>ann651
<Content>Loved It!!!! We recently got married and had flown to Maui to honeymoon and planned on staying at the PK for the night before we flew back to the main land. When we got to Maui, we hated the location of the cottage we rented and said Screw it so we flew back to Oahu and extended our stay at the PK from 1 night to 5 nights. In hindsight, that was the second best decision we made right after our first decision to get married in Oahu. We totally loved our time at PK. We really, really loved the band that played at night. We would sit on our lanai and just listen to the great music the band played which ranged from Hawaiian to contemporary songs. We so enjoyed the music that we spent out last night at the hotel downstairs by the bar to actually see the band play (we would have sat in the lounge chairs by the pool like we did the night before, but it sprinkled that night). Along with the music, we had a great view from our room of the pool and the street. Although we were not on the beach, I thought that our location was perfect because we could just walk across the street to the beach and there were so many places to shop and eat around us that we didn't miss the beach that much. The hotel is also next to the International Marketplace and we practically went there everyday to shop and eat. We totally loved the little sushi place in the food court at the Marketplace. It was cheap and the quality of the fish was awesome. Although we didn't eat at PK, we totally enjoyed our stay and the friendliness of the staff and the excellent location. Overall, we could not have asked for a better place to stay. On our next trip, we would definitely stay at PK!!! Plus it's a Starwood hotel so we got lots of points that we will definitely use when we stay the PK again.

<Author>Possomchops
<Content>Happy Chappie from Oz I stayed here for three nights whilst on my way to Canada from Australia. I found nearly everything pleasant and the location was practically on Waikiki Beach. I had booked a standard room but was upgraded on arrival to a part ocean view room/balconey. The hotel's buffet style breakfast was a bit too pricey for my budget so usually breakfasted at the Baskin Robbins icecream place come cafe, just down the road from the hotel. Prices for brekky (good sized portions) most reasonable at approx. $8 US, plus tax of course! The only gripe I had about the hotel was the lack of an electric jug to boil water for my early morning cuppa (being Aussie). A coffee percolator was provided which warmed the water but not hot enough for tea. I also noticed 4 hookers or 'ladies of the night' as we call them in Oz, just down from the hotel and was told that they 'hang out' there to attract Japanese businessmen who frequent the hotel. I found this curious considering that there was a police station just across the road on Waikiki Beach.

<Author>saskatoonguy
<Content>Great view, great room, great staff, lousy a/c I had a nice room on the 25th floor of the Ainahau tower, which is the tallest of the three towers. The room was very clean and I had a balcony. I noticed a chambermaid spraying disinfectant on the telephone and cleaning it with a small brush -- I was impressed and I wonder how many hotels do that as part of their regular routine. The decor was fine, and the view was unbelievable, of both the ocean and the rest of Waikiki. If you stay here, it might be worth paying more for a room with a great view. (Mine was described on the website as 1 king, ocean view, 282 sq ft.) Some cheaper rooms look onto a parking garage and nothing else, although those rooms probably get less exterior noise than mine.I thought the staff had a great attitude. I wish I could remember the guy who checked me in and checked me out, beause he seemed to genuinely enjoy interacting with customers. I wonder if some of the negative reviews here are because customers are reacting to the fact that the overwhelming majority of tourists are visitors from Japan and the people who live in Hawaii are overwhelmingly Asian-American. Deal with it or stay home.The location is very urban, which is what I wanted, with buildings packed together closely and the sidewalk at the front entrance. You cross the street to go to the beach. If you want a self-contained beachfront resort with more green space, try a place in western Waikiki such as the Sheraton Waikiki or the Hilton Village.Negatives: Some people might enjoy the free nightly show by the pool by a lounge singer, but it drove me up the wall! I hated the music. Even with my balcony door closed, the overamplified music reverberated through the room making it impossible to do things like watch TV, and this went on until 10 or 11. Noise from the adjoining room, filtering through a connecting door, was also a big headache even though my neighbor wasn't doing anything out of line. For some reason this particular block attracts prostitutes who are very aggressive toward solo male pedestrians after 10pm, even when in sight of police officers! My biggest gripe is that the room a/c was insufficient to cool down the room -- don't believe the nonsense about cooling ocean breezes (although I was there in August).

<Author>kelandtay
<Content>Best Bargain in Waikiki!! Stayed at the Princess Kaiulani again for this year's trip to Hawaii. Loved it as much as last year. This hotel has a beautiful lobby, nice pool area, rooms that go from small to large (some with a crappy view of the parking structure, some with a great view of Waikiki), and LOCATION, LOCATION, LOCATION at a GREAT price. If you're on a budget that allows for a mid-priced Waikiki hotel, choose the PK. If you want luxury, try one of the other Sheartons, the Halekalani or the Hyatt. Since you probably won't spend a lot of time in your room (which may be small but will be clean and have a parking structure that's close by and only 10 bucks a day for hotel guests), I'd recommend the PK! You can be on the sands of Waikiki beach in about 53 seconds after walking out the door of the PK, it's close to great shopping, an inexpensive food court is 50 feet from the pool, and, compared to other similar priced hotels in Waikiki, the Princess Kaiulani doesn't have that musty, old hotel smell.  I'll book another trip on Expedia NEXT summer and stay at the PK again!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>PK No Paradise in Hawaii My husband and I recently celebrated our 15 year anniversary in February and celebrated with a trip to Hawaii. This was our trip of a lifetime and needless to say that the hotel and location was a HUGE disappointment to us. Since the day we were married we often thought of this being our ideal anniversary vacation. WRONG. I have to agree with some of the other reviews, saying that the hotel staff catered to the needs of Japanese clients and made any American feel as if we were unwelcomed in their hotel. I would definitely say that I felt like a minority just walking around the lobby. Rarely would you see a smiling face, helpful person, or anyone speaking english without a HEAVY accent. I have no problem with other cultures or Japanese people but I do have a problem with how unwelcomed I felt.  The worst thing about this hotel is the location. I guess it's true that location means everything and this hotel really proved it to me. We had paid for an oceanview room and all we saw was one high rise building after the other. If you looked really hard, you may see the ocean between two other high rise hotels that were ON the beach. This is the LOUDEST place that I have ever stayed at and I felt very unsafe at night. We stayed in a higher room, second floor from top, and I could still hear music and noise booming until 1:00 a.m. I was looking forward to a relaxing, romantic trip and my nerves were on edge from no sleep whatsoever.  Oahu is a beautiful island, but I was certainly dissappointed in Waikiki. I will never stay in Waikiki again. Some people may love it, but I tend to hate commercial areas, and it has taken over. If you do go to the island of Oahu, spend most of your time on the NORTH shore of the island. This part of the island is gorgeous. Waikiki is too commercial and not the Hawaiin paradise I hoped for. One thing that I do recommend is the picnic basket that you can order from room service the night before. My husband and I took a picnic basket (which was absolutely wonderful and fresh) to the North shore for some privacy and relaxation, and it was the best day we had. We also had room service the night we arrived, and it was one of the best meals we had the entire trip. Another recommendation would be to go to Germaine's Luau. The staff was so friendly and it was an absolute blast. This is a great Luau and you can't leave Hawaii without going to one.  The Sheraton P.K. is a loud, unfriendly hotel with very limited accommodations. Don't expect much with your room. But I will have to say that my room was clean and consistently so during my trip. Dresser space was almost nil. My clothes were either hung(limited-no hangers/room) or in my suitcase. Positives- Room service, cleanliness and staff was friendly as you arrive in front of hotel. Unfortunately, that is where the friendliness ends as well. I hope if you are going to Waikiki that you will have your Hawaiin paradise. I was certainly dissappointed in mine.  
<Date>Jul 25, 2005

<Author>MissJen89117
<Content>Great stay! Would definitely go back. My boyfriend and I enjoyed this hotel very much. Being a Travel Agent I received an amazing rate that I certainly couldn't pass up. I mainly chose this hotel due to the location and star rating (compared to other places in the area and prices available for travel agents during that time of the year I planned on going). We were upgraded immediately to a partial ocean view room upon checking in, which was a nice surprise during all of the excitement of finally going to Hawaii! The area around PK is awesome if you're looking for a tourist hub -- relaxing when you want it to be and hustle-bustle if you want it to be. Hawaii is not only beautiful but everyone in Oahu was SO NICE to us. We felt completely pampered! Those working at the PK were accomodating, relaxed, and enjoyable. Japanese tourists definitely seem to rule the roost in Oahu - but we had no problems at all.. things weren't too busy tourist-wise. The AWESOME thing was, that this hotel offers a Hospitality Room/Suite for use by guests that have flights that depart late in the day. The room features a HUGE bathroom w/shower, sink, toilet etc, the sitting area has comfortable couches and lounge chairs and a coffee table, etc. You have the room for a full hour, which gives you time to shower and relax a bit before heading back out to catch a taxi to the airport. I would definitely stay at the PK again. I give it 4 stars out of 5 due to the excellent service and surprisingly easy trip.. everything went without a hitch and it made the trip well worth it --- This truly was a VACATION.$ Tip: Food in Hawaii is up there price-wise... depending on where you go, you can get some wonderful deals on Seafood.. so keep an eye out! Food cost wasn't too big of a deal for us since we'd saved so much money for the trip ahead of time, and we'd gotten such a great deal on the room.Tourist Tip: Go snorkeling in Hanauma Bay! Many tours are available for purchase at the Concierge desk... the agent working is more than happy to assist and answer questions. For less than $20 per person we received a bus transfer round-trip to and from the Bay, snorkeling equipment, etc. The only thing not included is your food -- you can bring your own food or purchase from their snack bar (pricey but ok when you're starving!). Keep in mind that there is a small additional fee per person to get into Hanauma Bay (as it is a state park and wildlife preserve).

<Author>travelcritic
<Content>The 'Last' Resort This hotel is in a great location, in between the International Market Place and just a short walk through the Sheraton Moana Surf, the beach. One thing you can come not to expect very much of in Hawaii is service so make sure you at least enjoy your hotel. The Sheraton Princess is one of the very few Sheraton's that doesnt utilize the Service Promise philosophy. The rooms were very basic, the walls were paper thin and the staff were very difficult to deal with. If you are looking in the budget priced hotels, I would entertain the Outrigger's as you can get some good deals on even the ones on the beach, the Outrigger Reef or the Outrigger Waikiki on the Beach.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>OK but Would look for Better Next Time First time in Oahu Hawaii, stayed at PK for 3 nights in May. Overall: Average. Ambience was pretty good, sometimes live night entertainment for their almost daily pool-side buffet (plenty of food and variety was great -- must have the SWEET pineapples!). Small-Med Pool is closed at night and early morning during breakfast time. Staff was nice and helpful. When we arrived, they had to fix double booking error (no problem). Our room was disappointing, old decor, and beds were too soft, and sagged in the middle. Clean enough, but not spectacular bath. 2 or 3 of our 4 lamps didn't work so we called down to fix, which they did while we were gone and surprised us with a nice complimentary basket of snacks. Balcony view wasn't great - got the side of a building. Lobby sells fresh leis for 5 dollars, which we took back on our 5 hr flight for family members. Location was pretty convenient: easy walk to the beach, and walked several blocks for shopping and other eateries. We went on one of those Bus Day Tours, and one shuttle tour. Our tour guides were great, but the tours were not...most of the time is spent on the road, looking out the window and about 5, 10 or 15 minutes at stops. Luau was fun (sorry don't remember the name), but we paid $100 ea. and it was about an hour drive to another beach on a bus (FUN RIDE, great people). Be prepared to tip every driver and tour guide you use (they expect it). TIPS: Recommend exploring sites on bus or trolleys and enjoy at your leisure. P.S. The Don Ho show - ok for seniors but pretty slow and dull for younger crowd.  
<Date>Apr 4, 2005

<Author>mamaknows
<Content>O.K., for downtown Stayed at the Princess from March 4 to March 13. The hotel is in a great location in terms of access to the beach and shopping. If you are expecting a typical Sheraton, you will be extremely disappointed. The outside of the hotel, lobby, bar, and restaurants all looked fabulous and the staff was very warm and welcoming. Shock was the room. VERY poorly maintained. Bedspreads are thin, decor is horrible, refrigerator barely worked, and the room was quite small. If the winds are blowing you will be up all night as the wind shook our balcony door so hard that it just continually rattled.Didn't feel as cheated the first 7 nights of the stay because I had a conference rate of $105/night, but it really hurt to pay $150 for the next two nights in the same room...I had no problems with parking and I thought that $10/day was reasonable. However, traffic in Waikiki is horrible so think twice about renting a car if you plan to just hang around downtown.Food was o.k., but VERY pricey. Dinner buffet at the hotel was 32.50/person and the breakfast buffet was 16.50/person. Both were good, but not worth the price.According to one of the Assistant Managers, the hotel is scheduled for an upgrade this summer, so if I ever go back, I might stay just to check out the difference. Your best bet is the Hilton Hawaiian Village (little further uptown) or the Sheraton Moana Surfrider which is right across the street.Also, be prepared for the Japanese invasion. I found that the staff seem to cater to them more than Americans. Most of the Japanese folks that I encountered were friendly, but a lot were obnoxious about cutting in front of you when standing in line and they seemed to have a real sense of entitlement--that did not apply to anyone else...  
<Date>Mar 15, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay My friend and I booked a great deal through Priceline.com. It was last minute- so I was nervous about it, especially after reading some of the reviews about the Sheraton Princess at Waikiki. It was the only hotel left. I'm glad we went ahead and booked and stayed. It was GREAT!!! The staff was very accommodating and knowledgeable. The hotel lobby area was beautiful and they had nightly concerts. The rooms are fine- not plush or anything but fine. We had a great view of the beach and mountains. The hotel even has a complimentary room for you to use if you have to check out and your flight doesn't leave until late. So- we freshened up prior to leaving for the airport. The best place to eat is the Diamond Head Market and Grill. It's nothing fancy and it's a to go kinda place but they have small tables outside. The food is the BEST! If you like ribs- GO GET SOME. They melt in your mouth. The Salmon and Ahi steak are really good too. For dessert try the Diamond Head Torte. This place is on the left going towards Diamond Head Crater. If you like hiking do that too. Peace.

<Content>Loved the Sheraton PK Yeah, it's a bustling place right in the middle of Waikiki, but that's exactly what we wanted on our first trip to Hawaii! This may not be the place for the Four Seasons crowd but we had an exceptional stay January 15-22, 2005. It was wonderful sitting on our balcony, sipping Kona coffee in the morning watching the sunrise and even better in the evening, watching the stage show from our very own private perch. My wife and I would definitely return to the Sheraton PK!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Keep Expectations Low Its a large hotel  that means busy and impersonal. The Japanese seem to like it and it caters very well for large groups of Japanese tourists who seem to be a permanent fixture in the entrance halls. The JAL crew are also accomodated here.The old Kaiuliani Wing is in dire need of renovation. Its quite clean, but definitely cracking at the edges. The courtyard rooms all overlook the multi storey car-park and rubbish bins (which are emptied daily at 6.30am beep beep!) It's not the most picturesque places.If you stay there as part of a cruise package, then you will definitely be in these rooms - be prepared to pay a hefty upgrade fee if you want a tower room with a limited view of the sea.It is in the middle of everything - if that's what you want, then fine. It is typical of Waikiki, but does not represent the rest of Hawaii which is a beautiful place. Waikiki is a god-forsaken concrete jungle!

<Author>maodohsiao
<Content>Great location, clean room at a great price I like the location of this hotel - it's right off the main street, the beach is literally 30 seconds away. If you are looking for a romantic get-away, this is NOT the place to stay. Go for Halekulani. But if you are looking for a comfortable accomodation at a great price, this is the hotel for you. About around $120-$150/night, there's not a lot of service to speak of, but it's a clean room and a clean bathroom - which is a lot more than I can say about some of the other hotels around the area (i.e. the various Ohanas). But if you want a nice swimming pool, this is not the place for you. Then again, the ocean is 30 seconds away. Why would you want to be sitting by the pool? I've been to Hawaii 4 times this year and stayed at PK 3 times...Next time when I go back, PK would most likely be the hotel I would stay at if I can't get a good deal at the Halekulani (which I LOVED, which happens to be twice, if not three times more expensive than PK)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani We stayed at the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani Hotel for 6 days in October. Arrived at 11am and were immediately provided with our room. As a Sheraton Preferred Guest I had booked the Standard Room rate of $119 with the limited view and was pleasantly advised that we had been upgraded to the 6th floor overlooking the pool. Rooms are dated but clean and provide all the necessities. Big problem is the neighbouring room noise. You can hear the television and EVERYTHING else (must have been honeymooners in room 626!!!). Great location and easy access to shops, restaurants, beach and transport. No need to take beach towels. These are provided for use by the pool and at the beach. Also provided are beach mats and chairs. Great service. Pineapple juice and freshly cut pineapple is served by the pool on Fridays. The best pineapple you will EVER taste. There is easy access to the beach via the lobby of the Sheraton Moana Surfrider and be sure to purchase your blow up rings from the ABC Store for about $3.50 and experience swimming with sea turtles each afternoon about 100 metres straight out from the Surfrider. We will definitely be back to the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani next year.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great service and a great stay I booked with the Princess Kaiulani through my Starwood Preferred membership and then stayed from Oct. 11-15th, 2004. While I was familiar with the PK and knew it was not up to the multi-star status of other Sheratons, I was not prepared for the terrific service I experienced during my stay. Traveling alone on business can be tiresome and a bit daunting for a female. However, the PK made my stay memorable. For instance: the hall light outside my room was out, but within 15 mins. of my call downstairs, an electrician was there fixing the light. On another occasion, the room hairdryer didn't function, and again within 15 mins. I had a new hairdryer. Repeatedly, whenever I needed something or whenever I had a problem or a question (directions, billing etc.), the staff was professional and accommodated my request. I also received an excellent rate from the hotel and was given 2 upgrades to a larger room with a partial ocean view.While there are inherent problems in the hotel (i.e. one has to walk through the dining area to go anywhere), there are an equal as well as greater number of advantages: excellent floor shows, no beach or pool towel nazis, helpful concierage, great room attendants (spotless room). I thought the PK was an excellent value and an excellent facility.

<Author>RBM1
<Content>Just okay We stayed at the Sheraton Princess over Memorial Day weekend for $119/night. We had some difficulty checking in with the $50 credit we got through spg--- (we are starwood members) - but the front desk staff was helpful and tried their best. It was the Starwood/Sheraton headquarters office phone number they called that was giving so much trouble. The hotel lobby is nice and the location is great - you can walk right across the street to the Sheraton Moana Surfrider out onto the sand/beach. However, the hotel rooms were not up to Sheraton standards by any means - they were pretty outdated - but it was a decent deal for $119/night. The walls were pretty thin also so bring earplugs. I would rather pay more next time to stay at a nicer hotel like the Surfrider across the street. Although I did not see the actual rooms, I assume with the higher cost to stay there that the rooms were in better condition and the lobby is magnificient.We had 1 meal at this hotel - the seafood buffet that wasn't really worth the price. With all the restaurants in Waikiki, I think you'd be better off there than at the hotel.On a separate note - if you love sushi, check out Sansei - they're in Honolulu but not right in Waikiki. Also, the Honolulu Coffee Co. is across the street attached to the Moana Surfrider, they had great coffee and breakfast pastries. A nice change from the usual Starbucks.

It's in central Waikiki so very convenient (near bus stops, beach, stores, eateries). It's kinda noisy but quiets down around 11PM. The hotel constantly has stuff going on (vendors, musical performers at night). Our room in the Tower was decent size, clean, comfortable (bathroom was nice size). We didn't eat there at all and didn't enjoy passing through the buffet eating area every time we had to get to the elevators, which made the lobby smell of food constantly. Really liked how they provided us with a hospitality room after checking out so we can freshen up and rest a bit. A good choice for a package.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Sheraton Princess was a Gem! We stayed at the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani Hotel for 2 weeks during July31-Aug.14th (2 weeks), and all I can say was, it was wonderful. Mind you, I did my homework before we booked with this hotel, I read all the reviews re: this hotel and I knew what tower to stay in before we booked. I heard bad reviews about the Kaiulani Tower and I knew I didn't want to stay in that tower. But I read great reviews re: the Princess Tower, so I knew that I wanted to get a room in that particular tower. Well, the first day we got there and the clerk booked us in the Kaiulani Tower which I refused to go to, but the clerk was really nice and managed to find a room available in the princess tower the next day. So we were to spend 1 night in the Kaiulani tower and then the following day they would move our suitcases to the princess tower which we wanted. Well.....the reviews for the kaiulani tower were right, the room was awful. We were on the 5th floor, balcony facing a dark parking lot, the room was dark, the room was so small, the bathroom was old and the beds looked really small and we were 4 people. The air condition was so noisey throughout the night, that we didn't sleep well at all. The next day, they moved us in later on in the day a the princess tower, wow.......what a transition......the room was bigger, we were on the 5th floor, facing the poolside and the street, the room also had a small couch and it was much more spacious and brighter with sunshine coming through our window. The air conditioner was newer and quieter, we didn't think it was on, thats how quiet it was. We stayed in this room for 2 wonderful weeks. It is our second time in Hawaii and we will be back for a third. We love Hawaii, the people are friendly and helpful and kind. But most of all we love the beaches, they are breathtaking. I'm hoping we go back in 5 years and I can't wait. I highly recommend this hotel, if you stay in the right tower, the people and staff are very friendly and really go out to make your stay comfortable. The service for breakfast, lunch and dinner are fantastic. The food is good too!A

What really threw me were the millions of TERMITES found crawling along the baseboards, in the light fixtures AND a few on the bed! This room is not fit for anyone to stay in!!! I immediately called the front desk and was moved to the newer wing on the second floor. It was somewhat of an improvement. The carpet and bathroom were clean. This should be indicative of how this hotel works!Take your money to another hotel. The newer rooms are OK, the older ones aren't fit to house even the prostitutes who can be found in droves on the side of the PK hotel. Go to the Waikiki Beachcomber instead.

<Author>mommyonvacation
<Content>Nice Hotel The Princess Kaiulani is fine. It is not a luxury resort but you will have a nice, clean room. The lobby and poolside lounge are very beautiful. The rooms look like they haven't been updated for a while but they are clean and comfortable. You're hardly ever in the room anyway. It is only a block from the beach and is within walking distance to many shops and resturants. I wouldn't advise upgrading to a partial ocean view however. When we got there, we were told that we had been upgraded as a courtesy. The view wasn't much, but we didn't pay for it so we didn't care. Looking straight out we saw the tops of the International Market Place. The ocean was mostly obscured by other buildings between us and the beach. We didn't have anything to complain about and our stay was fine. If you want to be really pampered in luxury this is not the place. But if you just want a decent place to sleep and be close to the beach, it's a good deal.

<Author>snokat
<Content>Hotel Princess K: Better than I expected! My husband and I stayed at the PK March 2  3 as part of a travel agent's package arrangements. We had just landed after an 8 hour non-stop flight and I was exhausted from a flu I caught the day before embarking. Thanks to the reviews here, I had some ideas when we arrived, like: drop off your luggage at the front door and watch them while your husband parks the rental car in the ramp. That way, you don't have to lug them down from the ramp. The bell hop/porter person was very good with service and friendly. Also, I learned that getting a Starwood card before leaving on my trip helped at check-in. The young woman was very courteous at the front desk. We were late checking in because of a HORRENDOUS car rental experience with Alamo (also set up by the Travel agent). I was dreading seeing the room and as we went down the hallway, I realized we were not in the newer tower part! But as we entered the room I was pleasantly surprised to find we were in a corner room and up high enough to watch surfers on Waikiki from our balcony! I nervously peeked into the bathroom and...glory be! No bugs! No mold or mildew! Everything looked like it had been scrubbed and was quite clean, freshly painted, wallpapered and the carpet looked shampooed! The beds were 2 doubles put together, but since my husband snores, I didn't mind- they were comfortable enough. My only complaint was the stupid street performers below and the terrible noise one of them made with his boom box playing such stupid lame-o music! His act was uncreative, untalented and dumb, yet he attracted lots of Japanese tourists for some reason. Even with the doors and windows shut and the heavy drapes pulled that awful music was blaring and finally stopped at 11:00 pm! With the Waikiki police station practically across the street one would think these pests could be controlled! Other than that, we enjoyed our time in Honolulu. The breakfast buffet was fine - our waitress was so nice and suggested fresh papaya for my tummy. It works! We ate in the hotel restaurant for dinner and the food was so-so. Someone earlier mentioned that they cater to Japanese tourists and I think I agree, but that is the case ALL over Honolulu!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Treated well February 18, 2004. Stayed at the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani for our last night on the Hawaiian Islands. This hotel is located in a very nice location in Waikiki and was very busy. This said we were treated very well when we checked in and the Bell Person brought us our luggage must faster then I had expected (seeing the pile of luggage outside when we arrived). The rooms were small and a bit musty smelling but we were upgraded to an Ocean View for some reason (Maybe because I am a Starwood Preferred Guest). This gave us a balcony overlooking the pool and the ocean could be seen over the other hotels. One of the best perks we were provided and I have never been offered anywhere else was the availability of a hospitality room. Checkout was at 11:00 and they could not extend it because they were in a sold out state, however, they offered us a room that we could check out and use for 1 hour to shower and clean up before we had to leave for the airport. We arrived at 2:30 pm after going to the beach and were able to get prepared for our trip home. The eight hour flight was much more tolerable. I would definitely stay here again.

<Content>I must not have been at the same place! I stayed at the PK January 20th - 24th and had a very pleasant experience. I wouldn't rate my room an A+, but it was a good solid B which is what I expected given the moderate price. I really enjoyed the central location and its proximity to the International Market. I never ate at the PK other than 1 room service breakfast that was quite good so I can't comment on their buffet (I don't like buffets anyway). The staff was very friendly and helpful and I really enjoyed the pool the one time I used it. If I were travelling with someone else to share the room cost, I probably wouldn't stay at the PK, but given the price and location I would stay there again on a solo trip like this one.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disappointment is an understatement Just returned from a stay at the Kaiulani from Jan. 17-21. We weren't expecting much given the reviews on this site, however, I was hoping that with the Sheraton name we could at least expect a minimum level of quality. Boy were we wrong. The room was small and old, as most other report. The meals at the buffet were horrible. I know not to expect too much from buffets, but we stayed at other hotels in Honolulu and Maui and the Sheraton's food was pure slop in comparison. The pool was small and poorly located. (Though this might not be a concern given the location of the beach across the street. Also, if you are traveling with children (or even if you aren't), be prepared for the hordes of prostitutes that hang out in this area every night. While it didn't feel dangerous, it wasn't exactly the environment that we were looking for. Overall, you're travel expenditures are better off being spent elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Kaiulani-Thumbs UP! We stayed at the Princess Kaiulani from January 15-18, 2004. We received an upgrade from a standard room to a room with an ocean view without any problem. The room itself was fine, the bathroom appeared to have been recently remodeled. The room was clean although the carpet appeared worn in a couple spots and also had a couple stains. The staff was very courteous and prompt. Maintenance was called to our room once and the problem was corrected quickly, we also received a call from the hotel apologizing. I thought the food was overpriced within the hotel and only ate lunch there once. There are a variety of restaurants to choose from that are near the hotel. Overall, I would recommend the Kaiulani.
